# NASP Abstracts and Posters 2019-2025

## 2019 / 01 / Patiromer and Maintenance of RAASi Therapy in Hyperkalemic Medicare Patients

- PDF: nasp_abstracts_posters_pdfs_2019_2025/01_2019.pdf
- Source: https://naspnet.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/01/01.pdf
- Categories: Access & Affordability, Adherence & Persistence, Clinical Outcomes, Real-World Evidence & Analytics
- Therapy areas: Oncology, Neurology, Cardiometabolic, Renal

* Patiromer cohort showed the highest percentage of patients continuing on RAASi therapy over a 6-month period. * Down-titration of RAASi dose in all three cohorts was low (~10%).

## 2019 / 10 / Penn University of Pennsylvania logo Appropriate Prescribing of Antiemetics with Oral Oncolytic Therapy, a Single Center Experience Penn University of Pennsylvania logo

- PDF: nasp_abstracts_posters_pdfs_2019_2025/10_2019.pdf
- Source: https://naspnet.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/01/10.pdf
- Categories: Access & Affordability, Adherence & Persistence, Clinical Outcomes, Health-System Specialty Pharmacy, Operations & Quality, Patient Experience & Support, Real-World Evidence & Analytics, Workforce & Education
- Therapy areas: Oncology, Neurology

* OOT is an increasingly common therapy with unique risks associated with prescribing practices. * Developing a program to increase pharmacist involvement with prescribing and counseling of oral chemotherapy harnessing the existing electronic health record. * Metrics to be measured as part of this program include appropriate supportive care medications, hospitalizations and quality of life.

## 2019 / 11 / Variation in health plan specialty drug coverage: An empirical analysis

- PDF: nasp_abstracts_posters_pdfs_2019_2025/11_2019.pdf
- Source: https://naspnet.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/01/11.pdf
- Categories: Access & Affordability, Clinical Outcomes, Real-World Evidence & Analytics
- Therapy areas: Neurology

Ø Overall, health plans applied restrictions in roughly half of their specialty drug coverage decisions. Ø We found notable variation in the frequency that health plans applied restrictions in their coverage decisions. Ø We also found notable variation in the frequency that health plans applied different types of restrictions in their coverage decisions. Ø Few drug-indication pairs were covered the same way by all included plans.

## 2019 / 12 / DEVELOPMENT OF A PHARMACY COLLABORATIVE PRACTICE AGREEMENT TO IMPROVE EFFICIENCY AND MANAGEMENT OF PRESCRIBING IN A RENAL TRANSPLANT CLINIC

- PDF: nasp_abstracts_posters_pdfs_2019_2025/12_2019.pdf
- Source: https://naspnet.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/01/12.pdf
- Categories: Adherence & Persistence, Clinical Outcomes, Health-System Specialty Pharmacy, Operations & Quality, Real-World Evidence & Analytics, Workforce & Education
- Therapy areas: Neurology, Infectious Disease, Renal

Implementing a CPPA resulted in: * Increased prescription volume * Reduced physician and nurse burden * Pharmacy growth from 8 to 24 team members * No safety concerns reported in seven quarterly reviews This streamlined process from prescribing to dispensing prescriptions ensures close monitoring of post-transplant patients, while allowing physicians and nurses to dedicate more time to focus on patient care.

## 2019 / 14 / Coupling Patient Care Management Operations with Technology and Data Platform to Optimize Hepatitis C Therapy Outcomes

- PDF: nasp_abstracts_posters_pdfs_2019_2025/14_2019.pdf
- Source: https://naspnet.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/01/14.pdf
- Categories: Access & Affordability, Adherence & Persistence, Clinical Outcomes, Health-System Specialty Pharmacy, Operations & Quality, Patient Experience & Support, Real-World Evidence & Analytics, Workforce & Education
- Therapy areas: Neurology, Infectious Disease

In this observational study of standardized clinical pharmacy operations provided in a medical clinic supported by a pharmacy technology platform it was demonstrated that the pharmacy care process can be streamlined between the numerous steps and become a dynamic patient management operation. In addition, the study demonstrated that an intuitive and robust data platform can greatly improve longitudinal follow-up and HCV cure rate measurement. References \* “Hepatitis C Guidance 2018 Update: AASLD-IDSA Recommendatio

## 2019 / 15 / Clinical impact of pharmacist interventions on improving outcomes in patients receiving immune globulin therapy in a home setting

- PDF: nasp_abstracts_posters_pdfs_2019_2025/15_2019.pdf
- Source: https://naspnet.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/01/15.pdf
- Categories: Adherence & Persistence, Clinical Outcomes, Health-System Specialty Pharmacy, Operations & Quality, Real-World Evidence & Analytics, Workforce & Education
- Therapy areas: Unclassified

Pharmacists can have a significant impact on preventing or reducing ADRs associated with IG therapy. In addition, the interventions suggested by the pharmacist have a high acceptance rate by prescribers and a positive effect on preventing recurrence of ADRs.

## 2019 / 23 / 23

* Implementation of an internal checking tool of oral oncolytics creates a standardized safety check and promotes active communication with oncology care teams. * Oral oncolytic therapy pose high risk to patient safety and an increase of standardized checking is required to minimize errors. * Expanding the double check process to include all oral oncolytic agents is ongoing; however, requires resources to allow for pharmacist dedicated time to provide clinical checks outside normal operation workflow.

## 2019 / 25 / Impact of a Specialty Pharmacy Benefit on Rheumatoid Arthritis Medication Adherence and Functional Status: A Continuation Study

- PDF: nasp_abstracts_posters_pdfs_2019_2025/25_2019.pdf
- Source: https://naspnet.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/01/25.pdf
- Categories: Access & Affordability, Adherence & Persistence, Clinical Outcomes, Health-System Specialty Pharmacy, Operations & Quality, Patient Experience & Support, Real-World Evidence & Analytics, Workforce & Education
- Therapy areas: Oncology, Inflammatory & Autoimmune, Neurology

* PDC is significantly correlated to HAQ-II scores at baseline. * Adherence is shown to increase for members transitioning from a non-specialty to specialty pharmacy. * Efforts must be focused on helping maintain desired adherence rates in patients with RA to have a continued benefit on functional disease status. * More analysis is needed to determine if the HAQ-II is an appropriate functionality questionnaire to assess RA disease status.

## 2019 / 26 / Economic Burden of Hemophilia B in the US: A Systematic Literature Review

- PDF: nasp_abstracts_posters_pdfs_2019_2025/26_2019.pdf
- Source: https://naspnet.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/01/26.pdf
- Categories: Access & Affordability, Clinical Outcomes, Health-System Specialty Pharmacy, Real-World Evidence & Analytics
- Therapy areas: Neurology, Rare Disease

* This systematic literature review found substantial economic burden associated with HB in the US. Mean annual clotting factor cost of HB management was found to range from $230,000 to $577,363 for a patient on SHL treatment and from $454,000 to $925,864 for those on EHLs. * The significant costs and health resources utilized by patients highlight unmet medical needs remaining in HB management.

## 2019 / 30 / Comparison of Extended to Standard Half-life Factor VIII Therapy in Patients with Hemophilia A on Prophylactic Treatment: A Retrospective Study to Evaluate the Efficacy, Safety, Cost, and Utilization of Treatment

- PDF: nasp_abstracts_posters_pdfs_2019_2025/30_2019.pdf
- Source: https://naspnet.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/01/30.pdf
- Categories: Access & Affordability, Clinical Outcomes, Health-System Specialty Pharmacy, Operations & Quality, Patient Experience & Support, Real-World Evidence & Analytics
- Therapy areas: Neurology, Rare Disease

Hemophilia A is a genetic bleeding disorder caused by a deficiency in factor VIII (FVIII). FVIII maintains bleeding homeostasis within the body through its downstream effects on the intrinsic clotting mechanism. The extent of the disease – either mild, moderate, or severe – depends on the amount of available FVIII in the blood. Patients with severe disease (FVIII levels 1 Treatment of hemophilia A involves replacing FVIII through either on-demand or prophylactic infusion therapy. While on-demand treatment is infuse

## 2019 / 34 / Estimating the value of pharmacist interventions in a specialty pharmacy setting

- PDF: nasp_abstracts_posters_pdfs_2019_2025/34_2019.pdf
- Source: https://naspnet.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/01/34.pdf
- Categories: Access & Affordability, Clinical Outcomes, Health-System Specialty Pharmacy, Operations & Quality, Real-World Evidence & Analytics, Workforce & Education
- Therapy areas: Oncology, Neurology

* RPh interventions in a specialty pharmacy setting add substantial value (estimated between $174.38 to $318.75 per intervention) in terms of prevented prescription and medical costs * RPhs flagged 115 impacts out of 14,441 interventions. This is likely an underrepresentation of the actual number of interventions associated with cost-savings through waste mitigation/resource reduction

* The algorithm by which PMN is traditionally defined grossly overestimates the true rate of primary medication non-adherence. * As only 18.6% of potential PMN prescriptions were true PMN, there is an inherent limitation in using only raw PMN as a quality metric for specialty pharmacies. * Overall, the rate of PMN for oral oncolytics at a HSSP was very low and mostly due to medication change, clinical decline, or patient decision.

## 2020 / POSTER-5 / Comparative Cost-Effectiveness Study of Hyperkalemia Management With Patiromer

- PDF: nasp_abstracts_posters_pdfs_2019_2025/Poster-5_2020.pdf

- Therapy areas: Inflammatory & Autoimmune, Neurology, Cardiometabolic, Renal

* For patients with hyperkalemia, a 27% reduction ($7220) in total mean costs at 6 months was observed for patients exposed to patiromer compared to patients who did not receive patiromer. * With 6 months of continuous patiromer therapy, the reduction in total (mean) medical costs (ie, inpatient, outpatient, and ED services) exceeded the increased cost to the outpatient pharmacy budget. * These results suggest that patiromer utilization may be a cost-effective therapy for the chronic management of hyperkalemia. * F

## 2022 / 50 / MR Fast: Assessing the impact of health system specialty pharmacy (HSSP) services on helping patients achieve Migraine Relief Fast

- PDF: nasp_abstracts_posters_pdfs_2019_2025/50-2022.pdf
- Source: https://naspnet.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/12/50-2022.pdf
- Categories: Access & Affordability, Adherence & Persistence, Clinical Outcomes, Health-System Specialty Pharmacy, Operations & Quality, Patient Experience & Support, Real-World Evidence & Analytics, Workforce & Education
- Therapy areas: Neurology

Health system specialty pharmacy services are effective at helping patients obtain rapid migraine control through therapy efficacy checks and beneficial interventions. * >90% of patients were on effective therapy by the end of the study. * The average time to migraine control was <84 days. * Majority of patients who did not have optimal migraine control at the first efficacy check obtained control by the next check. * Nearly all pharmacist interventions were accepted and proved to be beneficial recommendations.

## 2023 / 70 / Individualized Care Plans’ Effect on Therapy Adherence for Patients Prescribed Olaparib

- PDF: nasp_abstracts_posters_pdfs_2019_2025/70_Individualized-Care-Plans-Effect-on-Therapy-Adherence-for-Patients-Prescribed-Olaparib-_2023.pdf
- Source: https://naspnet.org/wp-content/uploads/2023/08/70_Individualized-Care-Plans-Effect-on-Therapy-Adherence-for-Patients-Prescribed-Olaparib-.pdf
- Categories: Access & Affordability, Adherence & Persistence, Clinical Outcomes, Health-System Specialty Pharmacy, Operations & Quality, Patient Experience & Support, Real-World Evidence & Analytics
- Therapy areas: Oncology, Neurology

* The Care Plan group had statistically significantly longer TOT (6.7 vs. 4.9 months, p<0.001) and lower risk of discontinuing treatment (aHR 0.77, 95% CI 0.64-0.94) compared with the control group. * The effect on TOT was more apparent among patients in the Care Plan group who experienced symptom resolution or dose modification. * These findings suggest the effectiveness of a nurse-led, personalized care approach for increasing TOT among patients receiving olaparib for treatment of cancer.

## 2023 / 8 / Smart Strategies for Control Room Temperature Shipping of Mail Order Specialty Pharmaceuticals

- PDF: nasp_abstracts_posters_pdfs_2019_2025/8_Smart-Strategies-for-Control-Room-Temperature-Shipping-of-Mail-Order-Specialty-Pharmaceuticals_2023.pdf
- Source: https://naspnet.org/wp-content/uploads/2023/08/8_Smart-Strategies-for-Control-Room-Temperature-Shipping-of-Mail-Order-Specialty-Pharmaceuticals.pdf
- Categories: Access & Affordability, Real-World Evidence & Analytics
- Therapy areas: Neurology

Phase Change Materials (PCMs) are not typically associated with low-cost cold chain solutions, as they compete with water-based solutions that have been used for decades. When controlling temperatures near 0°C, water is your best option regarding cost and performance. However, when the temperature requirement is at room temperature, a properly formulated and utilized PCM can far outperform water. This results in smaller, lighter, more efficient packaging with significantly reduced storage space and shipping costs.

Standardized adherence documentation and workflow will continue to facilitate patient follow-up for improved adherence.
